            function hasConnection() {
                return navigator.connection || navigator.mozConnection || navigator.webkitConnection || navigator.msConnection;
            }

            function createLink(src) {
                var preloadLink = document.createElement("link");
                preloadLink.rel = "preload";
                preloadLink.href = src;
                preloadLink.as = "font";
                preloadLink.type = "font/woff2";
                preloadLink.crossOrigin = "";
                document.head.insertBefore(preloadLink, document.head.firstChild);
            }

            var connectionDetail = {
                saveDataEnabled: false,
                slowConnection: false
            };

            var connection = hasConnection();
            if (connection) {
                connectionDetail.saveDataEnabled = connection.saveData;
                if (/\slow-2g|2g/.test(connection.effectiveType)) {
                    connectionDetail.slowConnection = true;
                }
            }

            if (!(connectionDetail.saveDataEnabled || connectionDetail.slowConnection)) {
                createLink("/static/fonts/HardingText-Regular-Web-cecd90984f.woff2");
            } else {
                document.documentElement.classList.add('save-data');
            }

    (function () {
        if ( typeof window.CustomEvent === "function" ) return false;
        function CustomEvent ( event, params ) {
            params = params || { bubbles: false, cancelable: false, detail: null };
            var evt = document.createEvent( 'CustomEvent' );
            evt.initCustomEvent( event, params.bubbles, params.cancelable, params.detail );
            return evt;
        }

        CustomEvent.prototype = window.Event.prototype;

        window.CustomEvent = CustomEvent;
    })();
</script>

    <meta name="dc.description" content="Sodium-ion batteries have not only garnered substantial attention for grid-scale energy storage owing to the higher abundance of sodium compared with lithium, but also present the possibility of fast charging because of the inherently higher sodium-ion mobility. However, it remains a phenomenal challenge to achieve a combination of these merits, given the complex structural chemistry of sodium-ion oxide materials. Here we show that O3-type sodium-ion layered cathodes (for example, Na5/6Li2/27Ni8/27Mn11/27Ti6/27O2) have the potential to attain high power density, high energy density (260âWhâkgâ1 at the electrode level) and long cycle life (capacity retention of 80% over 700 cycles in full cells). This study provides a principle for the rational design of sodium-ion layered oxide electrodes and advances the understanding of the compositionâstructureâproperty relationships of oxide cathode materials. The authors manipulate two categories of cathodes for sodium-ion batteries for a rational design that combines high energy density with high power density and long cycling life.">

        <div class="c-article-body">
            <section aria-labelledby="Abs1" data-title="Abstract" lang="en"><div class="c-article-section" id="Abs1-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Abs1">Abstract</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Abs1-content"><p>Sodium-ion batteries have not only garnered substantial attention for grid-scale energy storage owing to the higher abundance of sodium compared with lithium, but also present the possibility of fast charging because of the inherently higher sodium-ion mobility. However, it remains a phenomenal challenge to achieve a combination of these merits, given the complex structural chemistry of sodium-ion oxide materials. Here we show that O3-type sodium-ion layered cathodes (for example, Na<sub>5/6</sub>Li<sub>2/27</sub>Ni<sub>8/27</sub>Mn<sub>11/27</sub>Ti<sub>6/27</sub>O<sub>2</sub>) have the potential to attain high power density, high energy density (260âWhâkg<sup>â1</sup> at the electrode level) and long cycle life (capacity retention of 80% over 700 cycles in full cells). The design involves introduction of characteristic P3-structural motifs into an O3-type framework that serves to promote sodium-ion diffusivity and address detrimental transition metal migration and phase transition at a high state of charge. This study provides a principle for the rational design of sodium-ion layered oxide electrodes and advances the understanding of the compositionâstructureâproperty relationships of oxide cathode materials.</p></div></div></section>

            
                
                    
                        <div class="js-context-bar-sticky-point-mobile" data-track-context="article body">
                                
        <div class="c-nature-box c-nature-box--side c-nature-box--mobile" data-component="entitlement-box">
            <p class="c-nature-box__text js-text" data-test="access-message">

                <div class="main-content">
                    
                        <section data-title="Main"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec1-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec1">Main</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec1-content"><p>Lithium(Li)-ion batteries (LIBs) have played a crucial role in powering a wide range of consumer devices and contributed to the rapid growth of the electric vehicle market<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 1" title="Dunn, B., Kamath, H. &amp; Tarascon, J.-M. Electrical energy storage for the grid: a battery of choices. Science 334, 928â935 (2011)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR1" id="ref-link-section-d908765e590">1</a></sup>. However, the growing demand for environmentally sustainable and economically viable energy storage materials has prompted an exploration into alternative charge carriers that extend beyond Li ions. Sodium (Na), being abundant and economically more feasible compared with Li, positions sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) as a promising alternative or complement to LIBs<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 2" title="Yabuuchi, N., Kubota, K., Dahbi, M. &amp; Komaba, S. Research development on sodium-ion batteries. Chem. Rev. 114, 11636â11682 (2014)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR2" id="ref-link-section-d908765e594">2</a></sup>. SIBs are well suited for applications in renewable energy integration and grid-level energy storage, making them a viable option for achieving sustainable goals in the field of energy storage.</p><p>Beyond its material abundance, Na-ion presents two potential advantages as a charge carrier within rechargeable batteries when compared with Li-ion: a larger freedom in designing electrode structures and inherently higher ion mobility. The relatively larger ion size provides increased flexibility in the composition/structure of electrodes<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 3" title="Kubota, K., Kumakura, S., Yoda, Y., Kuroki, K. &amp; Komaba, S. Electrochemistry and solid-state chemistry of NaMeO2 (Me = 3d transition metals). Adv. Energy Mater. 8, 1703415 (2018)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR3" id="ref-link-section-d908765e601">3</a></sup>. The well-studied Na-ion layered materials, within the general formula Na<sub>x</sub>TMO<sub>2</sub> (TM: transition metal), can be categorized into two principal structural types, O3 and P2. Here, O denotes Na occupying the octahedral (O) sites and P represents Na occupying the trigonal prismatic (P) sites; the number 2 or 3 represents the oxygen stacking arrangement, ABBA for P2-type and ABCABC for O3-type, respectively (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#Fig1">1a</a>). Conversely, Li-ion layered oxides used in LIBs mainly crystallize in the O3-type structure<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 4" title="Mizushima, K., Jones, P. C., Wiseman, P. J. &amp; Goodenough, J. B. LixCoO2 (0<x<-1): a new cathode material for batteries of high energy density. Mater. Res. Bull. 15, 783â789 (1980)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR4" id="ref-link-section-d908765e612">4</a></sup>, for example, LiCoO<sub>2</sub> and Li[NiCoMn]O<sub>2</sub>. Interestingly, the additional P2-type structures typically provide enhanced Na-ion diffusivity and improved structural integrity, owing to the open prismatic diffusion pathways and the larger Na-layer distances between TMO<sub>2</sub> slabs<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 5" title="Fouassier, C., Delmas, C. &amp; Hagenmuller, P. Evolution structurale et proprietes physiques des phases AxMO2 (A = Na, K; M = Cr, Mn, Co) (xâ¤1). Mater. Res. Bull. 10, 443â449 (1975)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR5" id="ref-link-section-d908765e623">5</a></sup>. However, P2-type materials usually suffer from irreversible phase transformation at high-charge voltages (â¥~4.15âV), hindering higher reversibility<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 6" title="Talaie, E., Duffort, V., Smith, H. L., Fultz, B. &amp; Nazar, L. F. Structure of the high voltage phase of layered P2-Na2/3-z[Mn1/2Fe1/2]O2 and the positive effect of Ni substitution on its stability. Energy Environ. Sci. 8, 2512â2523 (2015)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR6" id="ref-link-section-d908765e627">6</a></sup>. Compared with Li-ion in O3-type structure, the larger Na ion has a relatively smaller ionic potential<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 7" title="Zhao, C. et al. Rational design of layered oxide materials for sodium-ion batteries. Science 370, 708â711 (2020)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR7" id="ref-link-section-d908765e631">7</a></sup>, reflected by a smaller charge density at the surface of the ion, which can lower the diffusion barriers, for example demonstrated by comparing O3-type NaCoO<sub>2</sub> with LiCoO<sub>2</sub> (ref. <sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 8" title="Ong, S. P. et al. Voltage, stability and diffusion barrier differences between sodium-ion and lithium-ion intercalation materials. Energy Environ. Sci. 4, 3680â3688 (2011)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR8" id="ref-link-section-d908765e640">8</a></sup>). Meanwhile, the larger Na ion contributes to reduced solvation energies in electrolytes<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 9" title="Okoshi, M., Yamada, Y., Yamada, A. &amp; Nakai, H. Theoretical analysis on de-solvation of lithium, sodium, and magnesium cations to organic electrolyte solvents. J. Electrochem. Soc. 160, A2160âA2165 (2013)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR9" id="ref-link-section-d908765e644">9</a></sup>, resulting in facile solvation reorganization at the electrodeâelectrolyte interphase<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 10" title="Barthel, E. R., Martini, I. B. &amp; Schwartz, B. J. How does the solvent control electron transfer? Experimental and theoretical studies of the simplest charge transfer reaction. J. Phys. Chem. B 105, 12230â12241 (2001)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR10" id="ref-link-section-d908765e648">10</a></sup>, thereby facilitating charge transfer and high ionic conductivities<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 11" title="Kuratani, K., Uemura, N., Senoh, H., Takeshita, H. T. &amp; Kiyobayashi, T. Conductivity, viscosity and density of MClO4 (M = Li and Na) dissolved in propylene carbonate and Î³-butyrolactone at high concentrations. J. Power Sources 223, 175â182 (2013)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR11" id="ref-link-section-d908765e652">11</a></sup>. These properties imply that Na-ion layered oxides have opportunities to develop high-rate electrodes. Despite extensive studies of various compositions, it remains a challenge for these layered oxides to successfully combine fast-charging capability with both high energy density and extended cycle life. The primary challenge is the detrimental phase transitions that can occur between O- and P-type structures during Na-ion (de)intercalation over cycling, compromising capacity and cycle life<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 3" title="Kubota, K., Kumakura, S., Yoda, Y., Kuroki, K. &amp; Komaba, S. Electrochemistry and solid-state chemistry of NaMeO2 (Me = 3d transition metals). Adv. Energy Mater. 8, 1703415 (2018)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR3" id="ref-link-section-d908765e657">3</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Han, M. H., Gonzalo, E., Singh, G. &amp; Rojo, T. A comprehensive review of sodium layered oxides: powerful cathodes for Na-ion batteries. Energy Environ. Sci. 8, 81â102 (2015)." href="#ref-CR12" id="ref-link-section-d908765e660">12</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Zhao, C. et al. Revealing high Na-content P2-type layered oxides as advanced sodium-ion cathodes. J. Am. Chem. Soc. 142, 5742â5750 (2020)." href="#ref-CR13" id="ref-link-section-d908765e660_1">13</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Zhao, C. et al. Ti substitution facilitating oxygen oxidation in Na2/3Mg1/3Ti1/6Mn1/2O2 cathode. Chem 5, 2913â2925 (2019)." href="#ref-CR14" id="ref-link-section-d908765e660_2">14</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Zhao, C., Ding, F., Lu, Y., Chen, L. &amp; Hu, Y.-S. High-entropy layered oxide cathodes for sodium-ion batteries. Angew. Chem. Int. Ed. 59, 264â269 (2020)." href="#ref-CR15" id="ref-link-section-d908765e660_3">15</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 16" title="Kubota, K. et al. Impact of Mg and Ti doping in O3 type NaNi1/2Mn1/2O2 on reversibility and phase transition during electrochemical Na intercalation. J. Mater. Chem. A 9, 12830â12844 (2021)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR16" id="ref-link-section-d908765e663">16</a></sup>, especially for the O3-type cathodes<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Kubota, K. et al. Impact of Mg and Ti doping in O3 type NaNi1/2Mn1/2O2 on reversibility and phase transition during electrochemical Na intercalation. J. Mater. Chem. A 9, 12830â12844 (2021)." href="#ref-CR16" id="ref-link-section-d908765e667">16</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Han, M. H., Gonzalo, E., Casas-Cabanas, M. &amp; Rojo, T. Structural evolution and electrochemistry of monoclinic NaNiO2 upon the first cycling process. J. Power Sources 258, 266â271 (2014)." href="#ref-CR17" id="ref-link-section-d908765e667_1">17</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 18" title="Ding, F. et al. A novel Ni-rich O3-Na[Ni0.60Fe0.25Mn0.15]O2 cathode for Na-ion batteries. Energy Storage Mater. 30, 420â430 (2020)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR18" id="ref-link-section-d908765e670">18</a></sup> which generally provide a higher reversible capacity, making them desirable for realizing high energy densities<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 3" title="Kubota, K., Kumakura, S., Yoda, Y., Kuroki, K. &amp; Komaba, S. Electrochemistry and solid-state chemistry of NaMeO2 (Me = 3d transition metals). Adv. Energy Mater. 8, 1703415 (2018)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR3" id="ref-link-section-d908765e674">3</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 11" title="Kuratani, K., Uemura, N., Senoh, H., Takeshita, H. T. &amp; Kiyobayashi, T. Conductivity, viscosity and density of MClO4 (M = Li and Na) dissolved in propylene carbonate and Î³-butyrolactone at high concentrations. J. Power Sources 223, 175â182 (2013)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR11" id="ref-link-section-d908765e677">11</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 14" title="Zhao, C. et al. Ti substitution facilitating oxygen oxidation in Na2/3Mg1/3Ti1/6Mn1/2O2 cathode. Chem 5, 2913â2925 (2019)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR14" id="ref-link-section-d908765e680">14</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 19" title="Mortemard de Boisse, B., Carlier, D., Guignard, M., Bourgeois, L. &amp; Delmas, C. P2-NaxMn1/2Fe1/2O2 phase used as positive electrode in Na batteries: structural changes induced by the electrochemical (de)intercalation process. Inorg. Chem. 53, 11197â11205 (2014)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR19" id="ref-link-section-d908765e683">19</a></sup>.</p><div class="c-article-section__figure js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="figure" data-container-section="figure" id="figure-1" data-title="Designing O3-type layered oxides."><figure><figcaption><b id="Fig1" class="c-article-section__figure-caption" data-test="figure-caption-text">Fig. 1: Designing O3-type layered oxides.</b></figcaption><div class="c-article-section__figure-content"><div class="c-article-section__figure-item"><a class="c-article-section__figure-link" data-test="img-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="image" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1/figures/1" rel="nofollow"><picture><source type="image/webp" srcset="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41893-024-01266-1/MediaObjects/41893_2024_1266_Fig1_HTML.png?as=webp"><img aria-describedby="Fig1" src="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41893-024-01266-1/MediaObjects/41893_2024_1266_Fig1_HTML.png" alt="figure 1" loading="lazy" width="685" height="414"></picture></a></div><div class="c-article-section__figure-description" data-test="bottom-caption" id="figure-1-desc"><p><b>a</b>, Structural illustration of P2-type (P6<sub>3</sub>/mmc) and O3-type (R-3m) structures. <b>b</b>, <i>d</i><sub>(OâNaâO)</sub> vs the ratio between <i>d</i><sub>(OâNaâO)</sub> and <i>d</i><sub>(OâTMâO)</sub> for typical P2- and O3-type oxides (Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#MOESM1">2</a>). Indicated is the relationship of both distances to the ionic potentials. <b>c</b>, Cationic phase map indicating the phase regions. <b>d</b>, XRD patterns of O3-type Na<sub>5/6</sub>Li<sub>2/27</sub>Ni<sub>8/27</sub>Mn<sub>11/27</sub>Ti<sub>6/27</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (R-3m, <i>a</i>â=â2.93945(7) Ã, <i>c</i>â=â16.3205(5) Ã, <i>d</i><sub>(OâNaâO)</sub>â=â0.32978ânm and <i>d</i><sub>(OâNaâO)</sub>/<i>d</i><sub>(OâTMâO)</sub>â=â1.54). The (1/3, 1/3, <i>l</i>) superstructure peaks at ~20Â° and 23Â° suggest honeycomb ordering of the Li/Ni/Mn/Ti sublattice. The detailed structure information is presented in Supplementary Figs. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#MOESM1">3</a>â<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#MOESM1">7</a>, Tables <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#MOESM1">4</a>â<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#MOESM1">7</a> and Note <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#MOESM1">3</a>.</p></div></div><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="article-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="button" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1/figures/1" data-track-dest="link:Figure1 Full size image" aria-label="Full size image figure 1" rel="nofollow"><span>Full size image</span><svg width="16" height="16" focusable="false" role="img" aria-hidden="true" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#icon-eds-i-chevron-right-small"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><p>In this work, we break from the established views by developing an O3-type Na<sub>5/6</sub>Li<sub>2/27</sub>Ni<sub>8/27</sub>Mn<sub>11/27</sub>Ti<sub>6/27</sub>O<sub>2</sub> layered cathode for SIBs through the rational composition design. The result is an exceptionally prolonged cycle life, evidenced by an 80% capacity retention after 700 cycles in full cells, accompanied by minimal voltage decay and enhanced energy and power density. Responsible for this is the incorporation of P-type characteristics, especially a large <i>d</i><sub>(OâNaâO)</sub> interlayer spacing of 0.33ânm within an O3-type structure. This design induces a predominant P3-type solidâsolution transition during charging, facilitating high Na-ion diffusivity while averting detrimental TM migration and phase transitions at elevated states of charge.</p></div></div></section><section data-title="Results"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec2-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec2">Results</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec2-content"><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec3">Designing O3-type layered oxides</h3><p>This study aims to develop an improved O3-type layered Na-ion cathode, leveraging its inherent structural and compositional features (see Supplementary Note <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#MOESM1">1</a> and Figs. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#MOESM1">1</a> and <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#MOESM1">2</a> for details). Here we selected a P2-type Na<sub>5/6</sub>Li<sub>2/27</sub>Ni<sub>8/27</sub>Mn<sub>17/27</sub>O<sub>2</sub> composition as a candidate to transform into an O3-type structure by minor compositional adjustments, because it has nearly the maximum Na content of known P2-type structure<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 13" title="Zhao, C. et al. Revealing high Na-content P2-type layered oxides as advanced sodium-ion cathodes. J. Am. Chem. Soc. 142, 5742â5750 (2020)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR13" id="ref-link-section-d908765e839">13</a></sup>. To attain an O3-type structure while preserving a large <i>d</i><sub>(OâNaâO)</sub> interlayer distance to induce high Na-ion mobility, it is crucial to reduce the bonding strength between TMs and oxygen. This will in turn lower the ratio between the <i>d</i><sub>(OâNaâO)</sub> and <i>d</i><sub>(OâTMâO)</sub> interlayer distances, thereby facilitating the shift towards O3-type stacking (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#Fig1">1a,b</a>). Here, <i>d</i><sub>(OâNaâO)</sub> and <i>d</i><sub>(OâTMâO)</sub> interlayer distances denote the perpendicular distances between the two layers of oxygen-containing Na ions and TMs, respectively<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 20" title="Zhao, C., Avdeev, M., Chen, L. &amp; Hu, Y.-S. An O3-type oxide with low sodium content as the phase-transition-free anode for sodium-ion batteries. Angew. Chem. Int. Ed. 57, 7056â7060 (2018)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR20" id="ref-link-section-d908765e868">20</a></sup>. Predictions based on the cationic potential method (Supplementary Note <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#MOESM1">2</a>), which relies on the weighted average ionic potentials of the ions, can provide insights into the P2- and O3-type stacking structures of layered oxides according to their compositions<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 7" title="Zhao, C. et al. Rational design of layered oxide materials for sodium-ion batteries. Science 370, 708â711 (2020)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR7" id="ref-link-section-d908765e875">7</a></sup>. Using this methodology, we find that introducing partial substitution of the redox inactive Mn<sup>4+</sup> with Ti<sup>4+</sup> should trigger the transition from the P2-type of the initial composition to the O3-type structure (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#Fig1">1c</a> and Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#MOESM1">1</a>). As evident from the phase map in Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#Fig1">1c</a>, the introduction of 6/27âmol Ti<sup>4+</sup> per unit in place of Mn<sup>4+</sup> results in a shift that crosses the boundary between P2- and O3-type phases, implying that the resulting composition Na<sub>5/6</sub>Li<sub>2/27</sub>Ni<sub>8/27</sub>Mn<sub>11/27</sub>Ti<sub>6/27</sub>O<sub>2</sub> in the O3-type structure should retain P2-like characteristics, in particular a relatively large <i>d</i><sub>(OâNaâO)</sub> interlayer distance. Laboratory X-ray powder diffraction (XRD) shows that this as-synthesized material corresponds to the predicted O3-type structure (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#Fig1">1d</a>), which can be indexed in the R-3m space group with unit-cell lattice parameters <i>a</i>â=â2.93945(7)âÃ, <i>c</i>â=â16.3205(5)âÃ, resulting in <i>d</i><sub>(OâNaâO)</sub>â=â0.32978ânm and a ratio of <i>d</i><sub>(OâNaâO)</sub>/<i>d</i><sub>(OâTMâO)</sub>â=â1.54 (Supplementary Tables <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#MOESM1">2</a> and <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#MOESM1">3</a>). Importantly, this O3-type Na-ion cathode has the largest <i>d</i><sub>(OâNaâO)</sub> interlayer distances among the reported O3-type Na-ion layered cathodes (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#Fig1">1b</a>), suggesting that this composition may promote high Na-ion diffusivity as discussed below.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec4">Electrochemical properties</h3><p>Electrochemical properties of this as-prepared cathode were evaluated within the voltage range of 2.0â4.4âV vs metallic Na (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#Fig2">2a</a>), which results in a high reversible capacity of ~152âmAhâg<sup>â1</sup> corresponding to ~0.69âe<sup>â</sup> transferred with an initial Coulombic efficiency (CE) of ~95% (Supplementary Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#MOESM1">8</a>). Moreover, this cathode has a high average voltage of ~3.5âV, primarily attributed to the Ni<sup>2+</sup>/Ni<sup>4+</sup> redox couple (~0.59âe<sup>â</sup>) and the oxygen redox (~0.1âe<sup>â</sup>). Upon oxidation, the voltage initially reaches a short plateau at ~2.9âV, suggesting a short O3- to P3-type transformation, followed by an extended region with a slope extending towards 4.4âV, which accounts for ~90% of the total capacity. Cyclic voltammetry (CV) shows a cathodic peak centred at ~3.1âV corresponding to the short plateau area followed by a broad peak associated with the extended sloped region (Supplementary Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#MOESM1">9</a>). When cycled at various sweep rates, the reversible redox peaks are observed, and the linear shift of these peaks shows the reversible Na-ion extraction/insertion.</p><div class="c-article-section__figure js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="figure" data-container-section="figure" id="figure-2" data-title="Electrochemical performance."><figure><figcaption><b id="Fig2" class="c-article-section__figure-caption" data-test="figure-caption-text">Fig. 2: Electrochemical performance.</b></figcaption><div class="c-article-section__figure-content"><div class="c-article-section__figure-item"><a class="c-article-section__figure-link" data-test="img-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="image" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1/figures/2" rel="nofollow"><picture><source type="image/webp" srcset="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41893-024-01266-1/MediaObjects/41893_2024_1266_Fig2_HTML.png?as=webp"><img aria-describedby="Fig2" src="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41893-024-01266-1/MediaObjects/41893_2024_1266_Fig2_HTML.png" alt="figure 2" loading="lazy" width="685" height="582"></picture></a></div><div class="c-article-section__figure-description" data-test="bottom-caption" id="figure-2-desc"><p><b>a</b>, Chargeâdischarge curves at 0.1âC rate between 2.0 and 4.4âV vs metallic Na. <b>b</b>, GITT curves for the first two cycles at 0.1âC, applying every 0.5âh (dis)charge and a 6âh relaxation period.The green curve presents the equilibrium potential of each relaxation. <b>c</b>, Chargeâdischarge curves cycled at various rates. <b>d</b>, Rate capability test from 0.1âC to 10.0âC. <b>e</b>, Discharge capacity retention, 0.1âC for the first three cycles and 3.0âC for the subsequent cycles. Inset: the discharge curves. <b>f</b>, Chargeâdischarge curves of the full cells paired with hard carbon anode at 0.1âC rate between 0.5 and 4.4âV. The capacity was calculated on the basis of the anode. <b>g</b>, Capacity retention of the full cells with 0.1âC cycling for the first three cycles and 3.0âC for the subsequent cycles.</p></div></div><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="article-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="button" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1/figures/2" data-track-dest="link:Figure2 Full size image" aria-label="Full size image figure 2" rel="nofollow"><span>Full size image</span><svg width="16" height="16" focusable="false" role="img" aria-hidden="true" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#icon-eds-i-chevron-right-small"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><p>The electrochemical behaviour was further studied using the galvanostatic intermittent titration technique (GITT) (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#Fig2">2b</a>). GITT voltage profiles display symmetry in both the charging and discharging cycles, while the initial two cycles show similar profiles, suggesting a high reversibility. Notably, three distinct thermodynamic regimes emerge, showcasing variations in voltage relaxation (Supplementary Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#MOESM1">10</a>). At ~3.4âV, this cathode shows a smaller overpotential of ~12âmV compared with the initial state ~2.7âV of ~100âmV and the highly charged state ~4.2âV of ~60âmV. This indicates a thermodynamic origin that might stem from different structural evolution and redox couples involved<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 21" title="Wang, Q. et al. Unlocking anionic redox activity in O3-type sodium 3d layered oxides via Li substitution. Nat. Mater. 20, 353â361 (2021)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR21" id="ref-link-section-d908765e1031">21</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 22" title="Berthelot, R., Carlier, D. &amp; Delmas, C. Electrochemical investigation of the P2âNaxCoO2 phase diagram. Nat. Mater. 10, 74â80 (2011)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR22" id="ref-link-section-d908765e1034">22</a></sup>. The smaller voltage polarization within the sloped voltage region indicates that this material exhibits a higher Na-ion diffusivity (diffusion coefficient of ~10<sup>â10</sup>âcm<sup>2</sup>âs<sup>â1</sup> based on GITT analysis) compared with reported O3-type cathodes<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 15" title="Zhao, C., Ding, F., Lu, Y., Chen, L. &amp; Hu, Y.-S. High-entropy layered oxide cathodes for sodium-ion batteries. Angew. Chem. Int. Ed. 59, 264â269 (2020)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR15" id="ref-link-section-d908765e1045">15</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 18" title="Ding, F. et al. A novel Ni-rich O3-Na[Ni0.60Fe0.25Mn0.15]O2 cathode for Na-ion batteries. Energy Storage Mater. 30, 420â430 (2020)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR18" id="ref-link-section-d908765e1048">18</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 23" title="Ding, F. et al. Using high-entropy configuration strategy to design Na-ion layered oxide cathodes with superior electrochemical performance and thermal stability. J. Am. Chem. Soc. 144, 8286â8295 (2022)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR23" id="ref-link-section-d908765e1051">23</a></sup>. This attribute probably contributes to the excellent rate capability and cycling stability (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#Fig2">2câe</a>). Upon increasing the current, the short voltage plateau disappears, leaving only a sloped voltage curve (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#Fig2">2c</a>). An electrode-level energy density of ~368âWhâkg<sup>â1</sup> is obtained at 5.0âC cycling rate, exceeding the so-far reported O3-type cathodes at the same rate (for example, ~269.1âWhâkg<sup>â1</sup> for NaNi<sub>0.12</sub>Cu<sub>0.12</sub>Mg<sub>0.12</sub>Fe<sub>0.15</sub>Co<sub>0.15</sub>Mn<sub>0.1</sub>Ti<sub>0.1</sub>Sn<sub>0.1</sub>Sb<sub>0.04</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (ref. <sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 15" title="Zhao, C., Ding, F., Lu, Y., Chen, L. &amp; Hu, Y.-S. High-entropy layered oxide cathodes for sodium-ion batteries. Angew. Chem. Int. Ed. 59, 264â269 (2020)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR15" id="ref-link-section-d908765e1087">15</a></sup>), ~286.5âWhâkg<sup>â1</sup> for NaNi<sub>0.5</sub>Mn<sub>0.2</sub>Ti<sub>0.3</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (ref. <sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 24" title="Wang, P.-F. et al. Ti-substituted NaNi0.5Mn0.5-xTixO2 cathodes with reversible O3âP3 phase transition for high-performance sodium-ion batteries. Adv. Mater. 29, 1700210 (2017)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR24" id="ref-link-section-d908765e1102">24</a></sup>), ~187.6âWhâkg<sup>â1</sup> for Na<sub>0.90</sub>Cu<sub>0.22</sub>Fe<sub>0.30</sub>Mn<sub>0.48</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (ref. <sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 25" title="Mu, L. et al. Prototype sodium-ion batteries using an air-stable and Co/Ni-free O3-layered metal oxide cathode. Adv. Mater. 27, 6928â6933 (2015)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR25" id="ref-link-section-d908765e1119">25</a></sup>), ~320.2âWhâkg<sup>â1</sup> for Na[Li<sub>0.05</sub>(Ni<sub>0.25</sub>Fe<sub>0.25</sub>Mn<sub>0.5</sub>)<sub>0.95</sub>]O<sub>2</sub> (ref. <sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 26" title="Oh, S.-M. et al. High capacity O3-type Na[Li0.05(Ni0.25Fe0.25Mn0.5)0.95]O2 cathode for sodium ion batteries. Chem. Mater. 26, 6165â6171 (2014)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR26" id="ref-link-section-d908765e1139">26</a></sup>), ~283.6âWhâkg<sup>â1</sup> for Na<sub>0.85</sub>Li<sub>0.1</sub>Ni<sub>0.175</sub>Mn<sub>0.525</sub>Fe<sub>0.2</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (ref. <sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 27" title="You, Y. et al. Insights into the improved high-voltage performance of Li-incorporated layered oxide cathodes for sodium-ion batteries. Chem 4, 2124â2139 (2018)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR27" id="ref-link-section-d908765e1158">27</a></sup>), ~183.3âWhâkg<sup>â1</sup> for NaTi<sub>0.5</sub>Ni<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (ref. <sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 28" title="Yu, H., Guo, S., Zhu, Y., Ishida, M. &amp; Zhou, H. Novel titanium-based O3-type NaTi0.5Ni0.5O2 as a cathode material for sodium ion batteries. Chem. Commun. 50, 457â459 (2014)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR28" id="ref-link-section-d908765e1171">28</a></sup>)), indicating a substantially enhanced rate performance. Moreover, the cycling stability of the prepared composition is remarkable, as demonstrated in Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#Fig2">2e</a>. More than 1,000 cycles were conducted at a current rate of 3.0âC (660âmAâg<sup>â1</sup>), with a capacity retention exceeding 88%. These properties give the present cathode material clear performance advantages compared with reported O3-type cathodes<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Kubota, K. et al. Impact of Mg and Ti doping in O3 type NaNi1/2Mn1/2O2 on reversibility and phase transition during electrochemical Na intercalation. J. Mater. Chem. A 9, 12830â12844 (2021)." href="#ref-CR16" id="ref-link-section-d908765e1180">16</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Han, M. H., Gonzalo, E., Casas-Cabanas, M. &amp; Rojo, T. Structural evolution and electrochemistry of monoclinic NaNiO2 upon the first cycling process. J. Power Sources 258, 266â271 (2014)." href="#ref-CR17" id="ref-link-section-d908765e1180_1">17</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 18" title="Ding, F. et al. A novel Ni-rich O3-Na[Ni0.60Fe0.25Mn0.15]O2 cathode for Na-ion batteries. Energy Storage Mater. 30, 420â430 (2020)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR18" id="ref-link-section-d908765e1183">18</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Mu, L. et al. Prototype sodium-ion batteries using an air-stable and Co/Ni-free O3-layered metal oxide cathode. Adv. Mater. 27, 6928â6933 (2015)." href="#ref-CR25" id="ref-link-section-d908765e1186">25</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Oh, S.-M. et al. High capacity O3-type Na[Li0.05(Ni0.25Fe0.25Mn0.5)0.95]O2 cathode for sodium ion batteries. Chem. Mater. 26, 6165â6171 (2014)." href="#ref-CR26" id="ref-link-section-d908765e1186_1">26</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="You, Y. et al. Insights into the improved high-voltage performance of Li-incorporated layered oxide cathodes for sodium-ion batteries. Chem 4, 2124â2139 (2018)." href="#ref-CR27" id="ref-link-section-d908765e1186_2">27</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Yu, H., Guo, S., Zhu, Y., Ishida, M. &amp; Zhou, H. Novel titanium-based O3-type NaTi0.5Ni0.5O2 as a cathode material for sodium ion batteries. Chem. Commun. 50, 457â459 (2014)." href="#ref-CR28" id="ref-link-section-d908765e1186_3">28</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Delmas, C., Braconnier, J.-J., Fouassier, C. &amp; Hagenmuller, P. Electrochemical intercalation of sodium in NaxCoO2 bronzes. Solid State Ion. 3â4, 165â169 (1981)." href="#ref-CR29" id="ref-link-section-d908765e1186_4">29</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Xie, Y. et al. Energy Mater. 6, 1601306 (2016)." href="#ref-CR30" id="ref-link-section-d908765e1186_5">30</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 31" title="Wang, Q. et al. Reaching the energy density limit of layered O3-NaNi0.5Mn0.5O2 electrodes via dual Cu and Ti substitution. Adv. Energy Mater. 9, 1901785 (2019)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR31" id="ref-link-section-d908765e1189">31</a></sup>. Importantly, no obvious voltage fade was observed during long cycling as shown in Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#Fig2">2e</a> inset, in contrast to Li-rich layered oxides that compromise cycling stability and energy density<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 32" title="Eum, D. et al. Voltage decay and redox asymmetry mitigation by reversible cation migration in lithium-rich layered oxide electrodes. Nat. Mater. 19, 419â427 (2020)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR32" id="ref-link-section-d908765e1197">32</a></sup>. To further verify the practical application of this as-prepared cathode, full cells paired with a hard carbon anode were tested (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#Fig2">2f,g</a>). When cycled at 0.1âC, a higher energy density of more than 260âWhâkg<sup>â1</sup> (based on both the loading mass of cathode and anode active materials) was achieved. When cycled at 3.0âC, more than 80% capacity retention was maintained after ~700 cycles, demonstrating its promise for potential application.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec5">Redox behaviour</h3><p>Redox characteristics of this cathode were studied using a combination of X-ray absorption spectroscopy (XAS) and resonant inelastic X-ray scattering (RIXS) spectroscopy (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#Fig3">3</a>), demonstrating that the capacity results from the Ni<sup>2+</sup>/Ni<sup>4+</sup> redox couple and oxygen redox. As shown in Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#Fig3">3a</a>, the similar <i>K</i>-edge of Ni<sup>2+</sup>O indicates that the Ni is in 2+ oxidation state for the pristine material. Upon charging, Ni <i>K</i>-edge shifts to higher energy, approaching that of Ni<sup>3+</sup><sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> at 3.7âV, subsequently increasing to values that indicate oxidation to Ni<sup>4+</sup> at 4.4âV. Upon discharging to 2.0âV, the Ni <i>K</i>-edge returns to its initial energy of the pristine material<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 20" title="Zhao, C., Avdeev, M., Chen, L. &amp; Hu, Y.-S. An O3-type oxide with low sodium content as the phase-transition-free anode for sodium-ion batteries. Angew. Chem. Int. Ed. 57, 7056â7060 (2018)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR20" id="ref-link-section-d908765e1244">20</a></sup>. In contrast, the Mn <i>K</i>-edge spectra remain consistent with Mn<sup>4+</sup>O<sub>2</sub> throughout the electrochemical cycling (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#Fig3">3b</a>), indicating that it is electrochemically inactive. In line with these observations, the corresponding extended X-ray absorption fine structure (EXAFS) spectra demonstrate a shortened interatomic distance of the first Ni-O coordination shell and a lowered magnitude of the Fourier transform, indicating that Ni is redox active (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#Fig3">3c</a>), while the environment of Mn ions remains unchanged during cycling (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#Fig3">3d</a>). Given that the redox potential of Ti<sup>4+</sup>/Ti<sup>3+</sup> lies below 1.0âV in Na-ion layered electrodes, it does not participate in charge compensation within cathodes<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 20" title="Zhao, C., Avdeev, M., Chen, L. &amp; Hu, Y.-S. An O3-type oxide with low sodium content as the phase-transition-free anode for sodium-ion batteries. Angew. Chem. Int. Ed. 57, 7056â7060 (2018)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR20" id="ref-link-section-d908765e1269">20</a></sup>. The specific capacity associated with the two-electron transfer capacity from Ni<sup>2+</sup> to Ni<sup>4+</sup> is ~130âmAhâg<sup>â1</sup>, less than that of the observed reversible capacity, suggesting the participation of the oxygen redox. This is confirmed by the O <i>K</i>-edge RIXS (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#Fig3">3e,f</a>), where the oxygen activity is revealed by the appearance of an additional feature in the spectra at excitation and emission energies of 531.0 and 523.7âeV<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 33" title="Dai, K. et al. High reversibility of lattice oxygen redox quantified by direct bulk probes of both anionic and cationic redox reactions. Joule 3, 518â541 (2019)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR33" id="ref-link-section-d908765e1286">33</a></sup> upon charging to 4.4âV (as marked by red arrow). This characteristic appears in the fully charged state and disappears upon discharging, confirming the reversible oxygen redox.</p><div class="c-article-section__figure js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="figure" data-container-section="figure" id="figure-3" data-title="Charge compensation mechanism and structural evolution upon cycling."><figure><figcaption><b id="Fig3" class="c-article-section__figure-caption" data-test="figure-caption-text">Fig. 3: Charge compensation mechanism and structural evolution upon cycling.</b></figcaption><div class="c-article-section__figure-content"><div class="c-article-section__figure-item"><a class="c-article-section__figure-link" data-test="img-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="image" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1/figures/3" rel="nofollow"><picture><source type="image/webp" srcset="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41893-024-01266-1/MediaObjects/41893_2024_1266_Fig3_HTML.png?as=webp"><img aria-describedby="Fig3" src="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41893-024-01266-1/MediaObjects/41893_2024_1266_Fig3_HTML.png" alt="figure 3" loading="lazy" width="685" height="684"></picture></a></div><div class="c-article-section__figure-description" data-test="bottom-caption" id="figure-3-desc"><p><b>a</b>,<b>b</b>, XAS of Ni <i>K</i>-edge (<b>a</b>) and Mn <i>K</i>-edge (<b>b</b>) in transmission mode for the samples at different states. <b>c</b>,<b>d</b>, EXAFS spectra of Ni <i>K</i>-edge (<b>c</b>) and Mn <i>K</i>-edge (<b>d</b>) for the samples at different states. <b>e</b>, Ex situ O <i>K</i>-edge RIXS spectra for the samples at different states under an excitation energy of 531.0âeV. The red arrow indicates the oxygen redox feature. <b>f</b>, O <i>K</i>-edge mRIXS spectra of the charged 4.4âV sample. The additional peak indicated by the red arrow indicates that oxygen participates in the redox at the fully charged state. <b>g</b>, Operando XRD patterns recorded at a rate of 0.08âC between 2.0 and 4.4âV. The peaks marked by an asterisk originate from the casing of the Swagelok cell. <b>h</b>, Charge curves of representative O3-type cathodes. The vertical bar denotes the differentiation between O3- and P3-type phases. <b>i</b>, Operando XRD patterns recorded at a rate of 1.0âC between 2.0 and 4.4âV.</p></div></div><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="article-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="button" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1/figures/3" data-track-dest="link:Figure3 Full size image" aria-label="Full size image figure 3" rel="nofollow"><span>Full size image</span><svg width="16" height="16" focusable="false" role="img" aria-hidden="true" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#icon-eds-i-chevron-right-small"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec6">Structural evolution</h3><p>Operando XRD was conducted to investigate the structural evolution upon cycling and the origin of the electrochemical characteristics. As shown in Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#Fig3">3g</a> and Supplementary Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#MOESM1">11</a>, upon initial Na-ion deintercalation, the O3-type cathode undergoes a phase transition from O3- to P3-type structure, corresponding to the short voltage plateau. Upon further Na-ion deintercalation, the reflection of the newly formed P3-type phase continuously shifts to smaller diffraction angles up to ~4.25âV, corresponding to ~0.59âe<sup>â</sup> transferred, without the appearance of new reflections. Charging to a high state of charge results in the (003) reflection of the P3-type phase shifting to a higher diffraction angle. This phenomenon can be attributed to the oxygen redox. As the negative charge on the oxygen decreases, it has the opposite effect on the unit-cell evolution compared with the increased oxidation state of TM ions. This change in the charge state leads to a decrease in the anionic potential (<span class="mathjax-tex">\(\overline{{{{\varPhi}}}_{\rm{anion}}}\)</span>), resulting in the observed shift to a higher diffraction angle. The XRD pattern at 4.4âV indicates that the material retains the P3-type structure (space group: R-3m), with only variations in the unit-cell parameters (Supplementary Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#MOESM1">12</a>). To further investigate the structural information, high-angle annular dark-field scanning transmission electron microscopy (HAADF-STEM) was conducted at 4.4âV (Supplementary Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#MOESM1">13</a>). The results show a predominantly global P3-type structure with local narrow stacking faults. This suggests an approximate solidâsolution reaction across the voltage slope region. The largest volume change from the initial O3-type phase to the fully charged P3-type phase is ~1.8%, smaller than those of reported cathodes<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 18" title="Ding, F. et al. A novel Ni-rich O3-Na[Ni0.60Fe0.25Mn0.15]O2 cathode for Na-ion batteries. Energy Storage Mater. 30, 420â430 (2020)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR18" id="ref-link-section-d908765e1430">18</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 34" title="Voronina, N., Kim, H. J., Shin, M. &amp; Myung, S.-T. Rational design of Co-free layered cathode material for sodium-ion batteries. J. Power Sources 514, 230581 (2021)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR34" id="ref-link-section-d908765e1433">34</a></sup>. During the discharge, XRD patterns follow the same transformation back from the P3- to the O3-type phase, demonstrating a reversible phase transition (Supplementary Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#MOESM1">14</a>).</p><p>Almost all the reported O3-type Na-ion layered cathodes undergo a phase transition towards the P3-type structure upon charging. The charge curves of the typical O3-type Na-ion cathodes are reported in Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#Fig3">3h</a> to investigate the capacity contribution from both the sloped region and the plateau region. The vertical bars denote the transition between O3- and P3-type phases, separating the sloped voltage capacity region and the plateau capacity region on the basis of the reported structural analysis<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 15" title="Zhao, C., Ding, F., Lu, Y., Chen, L. &amp; Hu, Y.-S. High-entropy layered oxide cathodes for sodium-ion batteries. Angew. Chem. Int. Ed. 59, 264â269 (2020)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR15" id="ref-link-section-d908765e1446">15</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 24" title="Wang, P.-F. et al. Ti-substituted NaNi0.5Mn0.5-xTixO2 cathodes with reversible O3âP3 phase transition for high-performance sodium-ion batteries. Adv. Mater. 29, 1700210 (2017)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR24" id="ref-link-section-d908765e1449">24</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 25" title="Mu, L. et al. Prototype sodium-ion batteries using an air-stable and Co/Ni-free O3-layered metal oxide cathode. Adv. Mater. 27, 6928â6933 (2015)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR25" id="ref-link-section-d908765e1452">25</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 35" title="Wang, H. et al. Large-scale synthesis of NaNi1/3Fe1/3Mn1/3O2 as high performance cathode materials for sodium ion batteries. J. Electrochem. Soc. 163, A565âA570 (2016)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR35" id="ref-link-section-d908765e1455">35</a></sup>. The P3-type solidâsolution reaction can be considered favourable for fast (dis)charging because of the more facile Na-ion diffusion through the prismatic sites and the larger <i>d</i><sub>(OâNaâO)</sub> distance (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#Fig2">2c</a> and Supplementary Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#MOESM1">15</a>). Compared with typical O3-type cathode materials reported, the present O3-type cathode stores more than 90% of the total capacity in the P3-type solidâsolution region, which is held responsible for its enhanced rate performance. The structural evolution of this O3-type cathode was also investigated at a higher current rate (1.0âC), exhibiting a highly reversible phase transition between O3- and P3-type phases (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#Fig3">3i</a> and Supplementary Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#MOESM1">16</a>). Compared with the slower cycling rate (0.08âC), the <i>c</i>-lattice parameter contraction at the end of the charge disappears, indicating that at this rate the oxygen redox is not effectively activated due to the slow kinetics (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#Fig2">2b</a>). Furthermore, the electrochemical and structural evolution towards a lower discharge voltage of 1.5âV was also studied, as depicted in Supplementary Figs. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#MOESM1">17</a> and <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#MOESM1">18</a>.</p><p>The post-cycling structural changes were further studied to gain deeper insights. The XRD pattern displays a coexistence of O3-/P3-type phases in line with the inset of the STEM image illustrating alternating O3- and P3-type structures (Supplementary Figs. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#MOESM1">19</a> and <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#MOESM1">20</a>, and Tables <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#MOESM1">8</a> and <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#MOESM1">9</a>). Further examination using HAADF-STEM images confirms the preservation of the initial layered structure after cycling. In comparison with the typical TM migration in Li-rich layered cathodes in LIBs, no TM migration to the Na-ion layer is observed in this layered cathode. Upon charging for Na-ion extraction, vacancies form in the NaO<sub>2</sub> slabs, which can induce TM migration into adjacent face-shared tetrahedral sites within the NaO<sub>2</sub> slabs (Supplementary Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#MOESM1">21</a>). However, due to weak repulsive interactions, TM ions can migrate even further away from these intermediate tetrahedral sites to energetically more stable octahedral Na-ion vacancy sites. In the P3-type phase, which is readily formed upon de-sodiation, the prismatic Na-ion sites form polyhedra with elongated Na-O bonds due to the larger interlayer distance (Supplementary Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#MOESM1">15</a>), which is energetically unfavourable for TM migration. This is because these prismatic sites are face-sharing with adjacent [TMO<sub>6</sub>] octahedra, introducing a strong repulsive interaction. Thus, the P3-type phase suppresses TM migration, contributing to the high structural stability and reversible electrochemical properties as observed in this O3-type cathode.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec7">Introducing P-type motifs into O-type materials</h3><p>The structural transition upon charging of the present O3-type material, a dominating P3-type solidâsolution transition, stands out from known O3-type Na-layered cathodes. Considering the phase transformation behaviour of the reported O3-type Na-ion 3<i>d</i>-TM cathodes, three distinct categories emerge (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#Fig4">4</a>). The first and early-studied category represents multistep phase transitions, referring to materials where the structural evolution starts from O3 to Oâ²3, P3, Pâ²3, O3â³ and O1 upon charge (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#Fig4">4a</a>), such as O3-type NaCrO<sub>2</sub> (ref. <sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 36" title="Zhou, Y.-N. et al. Phase transition behavior of NaCrO2 during sodium extraction studied by synchrotron-based X-ray diffraction and absorption spectroscopy. J. Mater. Chem. A 1, 11130â11134 (2013)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR36" id="ref-link-section-d908765e1536">36</a></sup>), NaNiO<sub>2</sub> (ref. <sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 17" title="Han, M. H., Gonzalo, E., Casas-Cabanas, M. &amp; Rojo, T. Structural evolution and electrochemistry of monoclinic NaNiO2 upon the first cycling process. J. Power Sources 258, 266â271 (2014)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR17" id="ref-link-section-d908765e1543">17</a></sup>), NaCoO<sub>2</sub> (ref. <sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 29" title="Delmas, C., Braconnier, J.-J., Fouassier, C. &amp; Hagenmuller, P. Electrochemical intercalation of sodium in NaxCoO2 bronzes. Solid State Ion. 3â4, 165â169 (1981)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR29" id="ref-link-section-d908765e1549">29</a></sup>), NaNi<sub>1/2</sub>Mn<sub>1/2</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (ref. <sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 16" title="Kubota, K. et al. Impact of Mg and Ti doping in O3 type NaNi1/2Mn1/2O2 on reversibility and phase transition during electrochemical Na intercalation. J. Mater. Chem. A 9, 12830â12844 (2021)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR16" id="ref-link-section-d908765e1560">16</a></sup>), NaNi<sub>0.60</sub>Fe<sub>0.25</sub>Mn<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (ref. <sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 18" title="Ding, F. et al. A novel Ni-rich O3-Na[Ni0.60Fe0.25Mn0.15]O2 cathode for Na-ion batteries. Energy Storage Mater. 30, 420â430 (2020)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR18" id="ref-link-section-d908765e1573">18</a></sup>), O3-type NaFeO<sub>2</sub> (refs. <sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 37" title="Lee, E. et al. New Insights into the performance degradation of Fe-based layered oxides in sodium-ion batteries: instability of Fe3+/Fe4+ redox in Î±-NaFeO2. Chem. Mater. 27, 6755â6764 (2015)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR37" id="ref-link-section-d908765e1579">37</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 38" title="Susanto, D. et al. Anionic redox activity as a key factor in the performance degradation of NaFeO2 cathodes for sodium ion batteries. Chem. Mater. 31, 3644â3651 (2019)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR38" id="ref-link-section-d908765e1582">38</a></sup>), NaNi<sub>1/2</sub>Co<sub>1/2</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (ref. <sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 39" title="Vassilaras, P. et al. Electrochemical properties and structural evolution of O3-type layered sodium mixed transition metal oxides with trivalent nickel. J. Mater. Chem. A 5, 4596â4606 (2017)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR39" id="ref-link-section-d908765e1593">39</a></sup>), NaNi<sub>1/3</sub>Fe<sub>1/3</sub>Mn<sub>1/3</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (ref. <sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 30" title="Xie, Y. et al. In operando XRD and TXM study on the metastable structure change of NaNi1/3Fe1/3Mn1/3O2 under electrochemical sodium-ion intercalation. Adv. Energy Mater. 6, 1601306 (2016)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR30" id="ref-link-section-d908765e1605">30</a></sup>), Na<sub>0.9</sub>Cu<sub>0.22</sub>Fe<sub>0.30</sub>Mn<sub>0.48</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (ref. <sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 25" title="Mu, L. et al. Prototype sodium-ion batteries using an air-stable and Co/Ni-free O3-layered metal oxide cathode. Adv. Mater. 27, 6928â6933 (2015)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR25" id="ref-link-section-d908765e1620">25</a></sup>), Na(Mg/Ni)<sub>1/2</sub>Mn<sub>1/3</sub>Ti<sub>1/6</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (refs. <sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 16" title="Kubota, K. et al. Impact of Mg and Ti doping in O3 type NaNi1/2Mn1/2O2 on reversibility and phase transition during electrochemical Na intercalation. J. Mater. Chem. A 9, 12830â12844 (2021)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR16" id="ref-link-section-d908765e1633">16</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 31" title="Wang, Q. et al. Reaching the energy density limit of layered O3-NaNi0.5Mn0.5O2 electrodes via dual Cu and Ti substitution. Adv. Energy Mater. 9, 1901785 (2019)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR31" id="ref-link-section-d908765e1636">31</a></sup>) and so on. The complex structural evolutions of these materials usually compromise the structural stability and Na-ion diffusivity, typically resulting in poor performances. The second category is the O3-dominated phase transition materials, which maintain the O3-type structure during a large fraction of the charge capacity before transforming to the P3-type structure (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#Fig4">4b</a>). The small number of phase transitions in the voltage window from 2.0 to ~4.0âV results in good cycling stability and rate performance, which are gaining more attention. However, these materials typically experience TM migration that sets in over 4.0âV, resulting largely in voltage hysteresis. Examples include O3-type NaNi<sub>0.12</sub>Cu<sub>0.12</sub>Mg<sub>0.12</sub>Fe<sub>0.15</sub>Co<sub>0.15</sub>Mn<sub>0.1</sub>Ti<sub>0.1</sub>Sn<sub>0.1</sub>Sb<sub>0.04</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (ref. <sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 15" title="Zhao, C., Ding, F., Lu, Y., Chen, L. &amp; Hu, Y.-S. High-entropy layered oxide cathodes for sodium-ion batteries. Angew. Chem. Int. Ed. 59, 264â269 (2020)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR15" id="ref-link-section-d908765e1665">15</a></sup>), NaNi<sub>1/2</sub>Ti<sub>1/2</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (ref. <sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 40" title="Maletti, S., Sarapulova, A., SchÃ¶kel, A. &amp; Mikhailova, D. Operando studies on the NaNi0.5Ti0.5O2 cathode for Na-ion batteries: elucidating titanium as a structure stabilizer. ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces 11, 33923â33930 (2019)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR40" id="ref-link-section-d908765e1676">40</a></sup>), NaNi<sub>1/2</sub>Fe<sub>1/2</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (ref. <sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 39" title="Vassilaras, P. et al. Electrochemical properties and structural evolution of O3-type layered sodium mixed transition metal oxides with trivalent nickel. J. Mater. Chem. A 5, 4596â4606 (2017)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR39" id="ref-link-section-d908765e1687">39</a></sup>), NaNi<sub>0.25</sub>Mg<sub>0.05</sub>Cu<sub>0.1</sub>Fe<sub>0.2</sub>Mn<sub>0.2</sub>Ti<sub>0.1</sub>Sn<sub>0.1</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (ref. <sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 23" title="Ding, F. et al. Using high-entropy configuration strategy to design Na-ion layered oxide cathodes with superior electrochemical performance and thermal stability. J. Am. Chem. Soc. 144, 8286â8295 (2022)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR23" id="ref-link-section-d908765e1708">23</a></sup>), Na<sub>0.7</sub>Ni<sub>0.35</sub>Sn<sub>0.65</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (ref. <sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 41" title="Wang, P.-F. et al. An abnormal 3.7 volt O3-type sodium-ion battery cathode. Angew. Chem. Int. Ed. 57, 8178â8183 (2018)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR41" id="ref-link-section-d908765e1721">41</a></sup>) and so on. The present material introduces the third category, P3-dominated phase transition materials, where the P3-type phase tends to form at the start of the charge and subsequently maintains as a solidâsolution reaction upon further charging (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#Fig4">4c</a>). This has advantages on structural stability, where the short O3âP3 phase transition at low voltages and the long P3-type solidâsolution transformation at higher voltages minimize strain from the volume change and TM migration, promoting a long cycle life. In addition, this P3-type phase offers fast Na-ion diffusivity, responsible for the high-rate capabilities. A comparison of the electrochemical performance of the three categories is provided as a spider chart in Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#Fig4">4d</a>. It demonstrates the appealing combination of cathode properties of the P3-type dominated phase transformation materials (Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#MOESM1">10</a>), supported by the plot of energy density vs power density in Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#Fig4">4e</a>.</p><div class="c-article-section__figure js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" A 5, 4596â4606 (2017)." href="/articles/s41893-024-01266-1#ref-CR39" id="ref-link-section-d908765e1787">39</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 41" title="Wang, P.-F. et al. NaCrO2 cathode for high-rate sodium-ion batteries. Energy Environ. Sci. 8, 2019â2026 (2015)." href="#ref-CR46" id="ref-link-section-d908765e1794_1">46</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Yue, J.-L. et al. Commun. 51, 15712â15715 (2015)." href="#ref-CR47" id="ref-link-section-d908765e1794_2">47</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Yabuuchi, N., Yano, M., Yoshida, H., Kuze, S. &amp; Komaba, S.
